## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically modifies elastic moduli and flow behavior, while strain determines the mechanical response through elastic, plastic, or hyperelastic constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally activated softening/stiffening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain in plastic regime)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (flow stress model)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elasticity)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature-dependent nonlinear response)
- Rubber/entropic elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to temperature, entropic spring)
- Neo-Hookean type: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) (hyperelastic with temperature scaling)
- Arrhenius-type thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Quadratic temperature dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (modulus with quadratic T dependence)
- Voce-type saturation: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Stress-strain slope is a function of T, often (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T) prefactor on strain terms
- Entropic elasticity (rubber-like) → Stress proportional to absolute temperature: sigma ~ T * f(epsilon)
- Strain hardening → Concave power-law form epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 for work-hardening metals
- Thermal softening → Monotonically decreasing prefactor with T, e.g., (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Stress-strain symmetry → For odd stress-strain response, only odd powers of epsilon appear (epsilon, epsilon**3, ...)
- Saturation stress → Exponential approach to plateau: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), stress levels off at large strain
- Phase transition / modulus anomaly → Non-monotonic temperature dependence, quadratic or higher polynomial in T
- Small-strain linearization → Leading term is always linear in epsilon; nonlinear terms become significant at larger strains
- Competing thermal mechanisms → Sum of Arrhenius terms exp(c/T) for diffusion-controlled vs. athermal contributions

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
```

With c2 = c5 = c8 = 316.1945..., let me call this value K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) - c4*T + c4*K + c7*epsilon**c6*T - c7*epsilon**c6*K
```

Grouping by terms:
- **T*epsilon**: -c0*c1 = -31.12 * 0.05295 ≈ -1.6479
- **epsilon** (constant part): c0*(c1*K + c3) = 31.12*(0.05295*316.19 + 1) = 31.12*(16.74 + 1) = 31.12*17.74 ≈ 552.07
- **T**: -c4 = -0.2255
- **constant**: c4*K = 0.2255*316.19 ≈ 71.31
- **T*epsilon^c6**: c7 = 3.6293
- **epsilon^c6**: -c7*K = -3.6293*316.19 ≈ -1147.2

So GT = **A·T·epsilon + B·epsilon + C·T + D + E·T·epsilon^c6 + F·epsilon^c6**

where c6 ≈ 0.5976.

The GT has these basis functions:
1. T·epsilon
2. epsilon
3. T

5. T·epsilon^c6
6. epsilon^c6

This is crucial: the GT contains **T·epsilon^c6** as a term. This means any matching candidate must have a term that can produce T multiplied by epsilon raised to a fractional power.
